data-emotion="css sz84eh">.css-sz84eh{margin-bottom:0.9375rem;margin-left:auto;margin-right:auto;max-width:min(calc(20.625rem * 2 - 1rem), calc(100vw - 1rem * 2));position:relative;}.css-sz84eh class="longform-container content-container article-container css-sz84eh e87de6m1"><style data-emotion="css 1qo10w8">.css-1qo10w8{padding-left:0rem;padding-right:0rem;position:relative;}@media(min-width: 48rem){.css-1qo10w8{padding-left:3.5rem;padding-right:3.5rem;}}@media(min-width: 48rem) and (max-width: (max-width: 100rem){.css-1qo10w8{padding-left:0rem;padding-right:0rem;}}@media(min-width: 90rem){.css-1qo10w8{padding-left:0rem;padding-right:0rem;}}.css-1qo10w8:after{clear:both;content:" ";display:block;font-size:0.7rem;line-height:1.5rem;height:0rem;visibility:hidden;}</style><div data-journey-body="longform-article" class="article-body-content article-body longform-body css-1qo10w8 ewisyje7"><style data-emotion="css 1nd4gv7">.css-1nd4gv7{font-size:1.1875rem;line-height:1.6;font-family:Charter,Charter-roboto,Charter-local,Georgia,Times,Serif;}.css-1nd4gv7 em{font-style:italic;font-family:Charter,Charter-styleitalic-roboto,Charter-styleitalic-local,Georgia,Times,Serif;}.css-1nd4gv7 strong{font-family:Charter,Charter-weightbold-roboto,Charter-weightbold-local,Georgia,Times,Serif;font-weight:bold;}</style><p data-journey-content="true" data-node-id="0" class="css-1nd4gv7 et3p2gv0">Ross Chastain was awed by skyscrapers.<br/></p><p data-journey-content="true" data-node-id="1" class="css-1nd4gv7 et3p2gv0">Addressing the NASCAR press corps Friday at the Art Institute of Chicago, the Trackhouse Racing driver and recent winner of the Ally 400 said what we’d all been thinking: “It’s a little different than Nashville, that’s for sure…For me it's a bit different than Alva, Florida, too.”</p><p data-journey-content="true" data-node-id="2" class="css-1nd4gv7 et3p2gv0">He looked out the window nervously.</p><p data-journey-content="true" data-node-id="3" class="css-1nd4gv7 et3p2gv0">“You can't see the sky. It's only buildings. I see a couple trees and from my point of view right now. I'm not used to that. I'm used to wide open farm fields and two lane roads in South Florida. When I strap in, I'm probably not gonna see much of the sky. It's gonna be buildings and, and walls and fences and, and tight confines.”</p><p data-journey-content="true" data-node-id="4" class="css-1nd4gv7 et3p2gv0">Chastain, a spicy, dynamic driver and the heir to a watermelon-farming family off Florida’s Gulf Coast, was right to be anxious. His anxiety was reflected everywhere the race touched, from the drivers, to the city government, to NASCAR itself, to fans, to the people who live in Chicago and commute downtown, their day woefully disrupted. I think it’s fair to call the Chicago Street Race, which took place Saturday July 1st through Sunday July 3rd, an experiment. A big, risky experiment. </p><section data-embed="pullquote" data-lazy-id="P0-8" data-node-id="5" class="embed"><style data-emotion="css 18qhvnb">.css-18qhvnb{text-align:center;margin:2rem auto 1.5rem;padding-top:0;padding-bottom:0;border:0.3125rem solid #E6B72A;}.css-18qhvnb:after{width:18.5rem;height:1.563rem;margin:0.625rem auto 1.625rem;content:'';display:block;background-repeat:no-repeat;-webkit-background-position:center center;background-position:center center;}.loaded .css-18qhvnb:after{background-image:url('/web/20240301153637im_/https://www.roadandtrack.com/_assets/design-tokens/roadandtrack/static/images/paddock-hr.svg');}</style><blockquote class="css-18qhvnb e1pe3zr91"><span aria-hidden="true" class="css-0 eagam8p0"></span><style data-emotion="css gwp8ws">.css-gwp8ws{color:#434343;font-family:GTSuperDisplayMedium,GTSuperDisplayMedium-roboto,GTSuperDisplayMedium-local,serif,Arial,Sans-serif;font-size:1.5rem;letter-spacing:-0.0225rem;line-height:1.2;margin:0rem;padding:1rem 1rem 0;}@media(min-width: 64rem){.css-gwp8ws{font-size:2.25rem;line-height:1.2;}}.css-gwp8ws b,.css-gwp8ws strong{font-family:inherit;font-weight:bold;}.css-gwp8ws em,.css-gwp8ws i{font-style:italic;font-family:inherit;}</style><blockquote class="css-gwp8ws e1pe3zr90">If the sport is to survive in the modern cultural consciousness, it needs to branch out, and fast.</blockquote><span aria-hidden="true" class="css-0 eagam8p1"></span></blockquote></section><p data-journey-content="true" data-node-id="6" class="css-1nd4gv7 et3p2gv0">For NASCAR, a lot was riding on this event going smoothly. The Street Race represents a bold new strategy, one that pulls from F1 courses like Monaco, capitalizing on a sport which is seeing a boom of popularity. It takes NASCAR, long considered a staple of the South (with all the cultural and political baggage wherein) and introduces it to a completely new, younger, and much more diverse audience. The diversity angle, namely the outreach toward Chicago’s Black community on the South Side was particularly emphasized by NASCAR’s community engagement events – for example, Bubba’s Block Party at the DuSable Museum of African American History. The message is clear: if the sport is to survive in the modern cultural consciousness, it needs to branch out, and fast. </p><section data-embed="body-image" data-lazy-id="P0-9" data-node-id="7" class="embed"><style data-emotion="css 20rem){.css-d9wkvk{margin:auto calc(50% - 50vw) 0.9375rem;width:100vw;}}@media(min-width: 30rem){.css-d9wkvk{margin:auto calc(50% - 50vw) 0.9375rem;width:100vw;}}@media(min-width: img:not(.ewcw41w1){display:block;width:100%;height:auto;-webkit-align-self:flex-start;-ms-flex-item-align:flex-start;align-self:flex-start;}</style><div size="large" data-embed="body-image" 1gccgwy">@media(min-width: 20rem){.css-1gccgwy{padding-left:1rem;}}@media(min-width: 30rem){.css-1gccgwy{padding-left:1rem;}}@media(min-width: 40.625rem){.css-1gccgwy{padding-left:1rem;}}@media(min-width: 48rem){.css-1gccgwy{padding-left:1rem;}}@media(min-width: 64rem){.css-1gccgwy{padding-left:1rem;}}@media(min-width: 73.75rem){.css-1gccgwy{padding-left:1rem;}}@media(min-width: 75rem){.css-1gccgwy{padding-left:1rem;}}@media(min-width: 90rem){.css-1gccgwy{padding-left:1rem;}}</style><div class="css-1gccgwy e1xqj1sx2"><figcaption class="css-1am3yn9 enfs9c50"><span class="css-cf5dap e6iqukd2">Michael Reaves</span></figcaption></div></div></div></section><p data-journey-content="true" data-node-id="8" class="css-1nd4gv7 et3p2gv0">Pulling from F1 is probably a good place to start. Jenson Button, 2009 F1 champion-cum-NASCAR driver, would know better than most. “I can only think of positives,” he said in the press conference. “We're trying something new…I know from previous experiences, street races for the teams, for the drivers, it's all a big learning curve.” For Button, Chicago is just the beginning. “I want to see racing in Europe. I think the European fans are very on board with NASCAR at the moment, especially after the performance that we had at Le Mans. They're new fans and I think that's one thing about racing in the streets here.”</p><p data-journey-content="true" data-node-id="9" class="css-1nd4gv7 et3p2gv0">That’s the drivers’ side of the story. For Chicago, the situation is more complicated. </p><p data-journey-content="true" data-node-id="10" class="css-1nd4gv7 et3p2gv0">The NASCAR Street Race was a project of the outgoing mayor, Lori Lightfoot, and since its inception has been criticized by community activists and transportation advocates around the city.</p><p data-journey-content="true" data-node-id="11" class="css-1nd4gv7 et3p2gv0">“We were deeply concerned about the lack of transparency here. And transit seemed like an afterthought. Safety seemed like an afterthought,” said David Powe, who works at the Active Transportation Alliance, a transit nonprofit. “The economy and tourism should never come before human safety, air quality and the equity concerns of making sure that people using the bus can get to where they're trying to get to healthcare, get to school, get to their medical appointments, get to a grocery store. We're just deeply concerned about the previous administration's push to get this approved and scheduled.”</p><p data-journey-content="true" data-node-id="12" class="css-1nd4gv7 et3p2gv0">“Chicagoans have been calling for better access to our public parks, whether that's Riis Park or Grant Park, Millennium Park or the Lakefront Trail. And [instead] we've just been giving more and more of our public space away to corporations. This is just another one of those examples,” said Rony Islam, an organizer with Chicago Bike Grid Now! </p><section data-embed="body-image" data-lazy-id="P0-10" data-node-id="13" class="embed"><div size="large" data-embed="body-image" class="align-center size-large embed css-d9wkvk e1xqj1sx4"><div class="css-uwraif e1xqj1sx3"><img alt="chicago, illinois july 01 chicago onlookers watch practice for the nascar xfinity series the loop 121 at the chicago street course on july 01, 2023 in chicago, illinois photo by chris graythengetty images" title="NASCAR Xfinity Series The Loop 121 - Practice" loading="lazy" width="4901" height="3267" decoding="async" data-nimg="1" style="color:transparent;width:100%;height:auto;" sizes="100vw" srcset="https://web.archive.org/web/20240301153637im_/https://hips.hearstapps.com/hmg-prod/images/gettyimages-1507331124-64a43dcba922a.jpg?resize=640:* 640w, https://web.archive.org/web/20240301153637im_/https://hips.hearstapps.com/hmg-prod/images/gettyimages-1507331124-64a43dcba922a.jpg?resize=980:* 980w, https://web.archive.org/web/20240301153637im_/https://hips.hearstapps.com/hmg-prod/images/gettyimages-1507331124-64a43dcba922a.jpg?resize=1200:* 1120w, https://web.archive.org/web/20240301153637im_/https://hips.hearstapps.com/hmg-prod/images/gettyimages-1507331124-64a43dcba922a.jpg?resize=1200:* 1200w, https://web.archive.org/web/20240301153637im_/https://hips.hearstapps.com/hmg-prod/images/gettyimages-1507331124-64a43dcba922a.jpg?resize=2048:* 1920w" src="https://web.archive.org/web/20240301153637im_/https://hips.hearstapps.com/hmg-prod/images/gettyimages-1507331124-64a43dcba922a.jpg?resize=2048:*" class="css-0 evyp0mv0"/><div class="css-1gccgwy e1xqj1sx2"><figcaption class="css-1am3yn9 enfs9c50"><span class="css-cf5dap e6iqukd2">Chris Graythen</span></figcaption></div></div></div></section><p data-journey-content="true" data-node-id="14" class="css-1nd4gv7 et3p2gv0">“NASCAR talks a lot about like, oh, I'm doing community outreach, and they've got like a section of their setup that's open to the public or whatever. But it's not really open to the public and it's not open to all Chicagoans. And when you look at their ticket prices, for example, oh yeah. It's very clear that it's not open to all Chicagoans.”</p><section data-embed="pullquote" data-lazy-id="P0-11" data-node-id="15" class="embed"><blockquote class="css-18qhvnb e1pe3zr91"><span aria-hidden="true" class="css-0 eagam8p0"></span><blockquote class="css-gwp8ws e1pe3zr90">"It’s giving Fyre Festival,” I overheard a fan say waiting in line for a $10 Busch Light.</blockquote><span aria-hidden="true" class="css-0 eagam8p1"></span></blockquote></section><p data-journey-content="true" data-node-id="16" class="css-1nd4gv7 et3p2gv0">Islam has a point. At $269 and up, the tickets, in fact, do not come cheap. Even for NASCAR, they’re deeply expensive, and the organization hoped that by combining the race with a kind of half music festival – acts like The Black Crows and the Chainsmokers were to perform – would justify the cost of entry. If NASCAR wants to reach out to a more diverse fanbase, $269 is a little high if you’re a college student or working a 9-to-5. </p><p data-journey-content="true" data-node-id="17" class="css-1nd4gv7 et3p2gv0">Regardless of the lack of transparency, the turning of Grant Park into a fortress, and the high costs, the event would go on regardless. The big experiment was on. </p><p data-journey-content="true" data-node-id="18" class="css-1nd4gv7 et3p2gv0">Then the flood came.</p><style data-emotion="css 18pb4rg">.css-18pb4rg{border:0;border-bottom:thin solid black;margin:1.875rem 0;clear:both;}</style><hr data-node-id="19" class="css-18pb4rg et3p2gv0"/><div data-embed="composite" data-lazy-id="P0-12" data-node-id="20" class="embed css-0 e18i9nfs2"><style data-emotion="css 1hgr6no">.css-1hgr6no{display:-webkit-box;display:-webkit-flex;display:-ms-flexbox;display:flex;-webkit-flex-direction:column;-ms-flex-direction:column;flex-direction:column;}.css-1hgr6no 61.25rem){.css-1hgr6no .e18i9nfs1:nth-of-type(2){margin-top:1rem;}}@media(min-width: 61.25rem){.css-1hgr6no .e18i9nfs1:nth-of-type(2){margin-left:1rem;}}@media(min-width: 61.25rem){.css-1hgr6no{-webkit-flex-direction:row;-ms-flex-direction:row;flex-direction:row;}}@media(min-width: 73.75rem){.css-1hgr6no{width:109%;margin-left:-4.5%;}}@media(min-width: 75rem){.css-1hgr6no{width:112%;margin-left:-6%;}}@media(min-width: 90rem){.css-1hgr6no{width:130%;margin-left:-15%;}}</style><div class="css-1hgr6no e18i9nfs0"><style data-emotion="css wwfqzh">.css-wwfqzh img{height:auto;}</style><div class="css-wwfqzh e18i9nfs1"><style data-emotion="css img:not(.ewcw41w1){display:block;width:100%;height:auto;-webkit-align-self:flex-start;-ms-flex-item-align:flex-start;align-self:flex-start;}</style><div size="medium" data-embed="body-image" class="css-cf5dap e6iqukd2">Chris Graythen</span></figcaption></div></div></div></div><div class="css-wwfqzh e18i9nfs1"><div size="medium" data-embed="body-image" class="align-center size-medium embed css-1736von e1xqj1sx4"><div class="css-uwraif e1xqj1sx3"><img alt="chicago, illinois july 02 crew members prepare the 43 draiver chevrolet, driven by erik jones during a weather delay the nascar cup series grant park 220 at the chicago street course on july 02, 2023 in chicago, illinois photo by chris graythengetty images" title="NASCAR Cup Series Grant Park 220" loading="lazy" width="5472" height="3648" decoding="async" data-nimg="1" style="color:transparent;width:100%;height:auto;" sizes="100vw" srcset="https://web.archive.org/web/20240301153637im_/https://hips.hearstapps.com/hmg-prod/images/gettyimages-1509828599-64a43cf95db1f.jpg?resize=640:* 640w, https://web.archive.org/web/20240301153637im_/https://hips.hearstapps.com/hmg-prod/images/gettyimages-1509828599-64a43cf95db1f.jpg?resize=768:* 980w, https://web.archive.org/web/20240301153637im_/https://hips.hearstapps.com/hmg-prod/images/gettyimages-1509828599-64a43cf95db1f.jpg?resize=980:* 1120w, https://web.archive.org/web/20240301153637im_/https://hips.hearstapps.com/hmg-prod/images/gettyimages-1509828599-64a43cf95db1f.jpg?resize=980:* 1200w, https://web.archive.org/web/20240301153637im_/https://hips.hearstapps.com/hmg-prod/images/gettyimages-1509828599-64a43cf95db1f.jpg?resize=980:* 1920w" src="https://web.archive.org/web/20240301153637im_/https://hips.hearstapps.com/hmg-prod/images/gettyimages-1509828599-64a43cf95db1f.jpg?resize=980:*" class="css-0 evyp0mv0"/><div class="css-swqnqv e1xqj1sx2"><figcaption class="css-1am3yn9 enfs9c50"><span class="css-cf5dap e6iqukd2">Chris Graythen</span></figcaption></div></div></div></div></div></div><p data-journey-content="true" data-node-id="21" class="css-1nd4gv7 et3p2gv0">Things weren’t ideal before it started raining on Saturday. “It’s giving Fyre Festival,” I overheard a fan say waiting in line for a $10 Busch Light in the General Admission Plus zone, which gave one access to a bunch of strewn about picnic tables and bathrooms that weren’t porta potties. Lots of things were already coming apart by the time I got there during the Xfinity Cup practice round on Saturday. Many fans, including myself, assumed that a GA+ ticket included a seat in the grandstands. It did not. Those were reserved for ticket holders paying a frankly insane $465 and up, and there was nothing indicating that spectators should bring their own chairs. The sophisticated Tap to Pay bracelet system didn’t work. By 2 p.m., when the first show started, Grant Park was virtually empty. I’ve been to house shows with more people. Things began to fill up when the Xfinity race started, only for it to be called off due to lightning strikes. The City of Chicago has a 90 minute waiting period for lightning compared to NASCAR’s 30. Eventually, everyone was sent home and the Chainsmokers concert was canceled.</p><section data-embed="pullquote" data-lazy-id="P0-13" data-node-id="22" class="embed"><blockquote class="css-18qhvnb e1pe3zr91"><span aria-hidden="true" class="css-0 eagam8p0"></span><blockquote class="css-gwp8ws e1pe3zr90">The grounds were one giant puddle, the sidewalks caked with mud. Honestly, I felt bad for everyone.</blockquote><span aria-hidden="true" class="css-0 eagam8p1"></span></blockquote></section><p data-journey-content="true" data-node-id="23" class="css-1nd4gv7 et3p2gv0">It got worse. Chicago has been suffering from a severe drought for months, only for the heavens to open beginning Sunday morning. Flash Flood warnings swept in around the city with explicit instructions: DO NOT LEAVE YOUR POSITION UNLESS YOU ARE SEEKING SAFER GROUND. Images from the racetrack started to pour (pun intended) in from Twitter. <style data-emotion="css kji66a">.css-kji66a{-webkit-text-decoration:underline;text-decoration:underline;text-decoration-thickness:0.0625rem;text-decoration-color:#668892;text-underline-offset:0.25rem;color:#000000;-webkit-transition:all 0.3s ease-in-out;transition:all 0.3s ease-in-out;word-break:break-word;padding-top:0.05rem;padding-bottom:0.05rem;-webkit-background-size:0 0;background-size:0 0;background-image:linear-gradient(rgb(239, 237, 233) 0px, rgb(239, 237, 233) 100%);background-repeat:repeat-x;-webkit-background-position:0 100%;background-position:0 100%;}.css-kji66a:hover{color:#000000;text-decoration-color:border-link-body-hover;-webkit-background-size:0.625rem 3.125rem;background-size:0.625rem 3.125rem;}</style><a href="https://web.archive.org/web/20240301153637/https://twitter.com/noahgragson/status/1675611785821409280?s=46&amp;t=QLFAOSre4djI0694ZNZveQ" data-vars-ga-outbound-link="https://twitter.com/noahgragson/status/1675611785821409280?s=46&amp;t=QLFAOSre4djI0694ZNZveQ" data-vars-ga-ux-element="Hyperlink" data-vars-ga-call-to-action="Tires floating in puddles" class="body-link css-kji66a et3p2gv0"><u>Tires floating in puddles</u></a>. Inches of water standing on the asphalt. First the hammer came for the musical acts. Then the resumption of the Xfinity Race, leaving Cole Custer declared the winner in a rare race called before the end of &quot;stage 2.&quot; All eyes were on the Cup Series, which entered a holding pattern at least until the rain stopped and the track could be squeegeed. In the replies to each news update were fans demanding a refund, as the musical acts and other perks were the only advantage they had over those folks crowding around balconies and peeking through the holes in fences. Cameras panned towards empty grandstands and drivers standing around in ankle-high water. It was, to put it bluntly, a disaster for NASCAR. </p><section data-embed="x" data-lazy-id="P0-14" data-node-id="24" class="embed"><div data-embed="x"><section data-lazy-parent="P0-14" class="embed"><style data-emotion="css 10klw3m">.css-10klw3m{height:100%;}</style><div data-embed="x" class="embed align-center css-10klw3m ez8lbhw1"><style data-emotion="css 63r9na">.css-63r9na{-webkit-align-items:center;-webkit-box-align:center;-ms-flex-align:center;align-items:center;display:-webkit-box;display:-webkit-flex;display:-ms-flexbox;display:flex;-webkit-box-pack:center;-ms-flex-pack:center;-webkit-justify-content:center;justify-content:center;min-height:10rem;background-color:#F5F5F5;color:#000;-webkit-flex-direction:column;-ms-flex-direction:column;flex-direction:column;height:100%;margin-bottom:0.9375rem;}</style><div class="css-63r9na ez8lbhw0"><style data-emotion="css 1msakm2">.css-1msakm2{width:3.125rem;height:3.125rem;}</style><img data-dynamic-svg="true" src="/web/20240301153637im_/https://www.roadandtrack.com/_assets/design-tokens/fre/static/icons/social/x.3361b6d.svg?primary=currentColor&amp;id=link-out-embed" loading="lazy" data-testid="dynamic-svg-base" height="auto" width="auto" alt="x" class="css-1msakm2 ez8lbhw2"/><a target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20240301153637/https://twitter.com/noahgragson/status/1675611785821409280?s=46&amp;t=QLFAOSre4djI0694ZNZveQ" aria-label="View full post on X" class="css-0 e1c1bym14">View full post on X</a></div></div></section></div></section><p data-journey-content="true" data-node-id="25" class="css-1nd4gv7 et3p2gv0">When the news came that they’d try to race – doing a few single-file laps under caution to give the drivers the final say – the sun emerged from the clouds. By the time I got down to the track, people had gathered in ponchos, skeptical and burned out. The grounds were one giant puddle, the sidewalks caked with mud. Honestly, I felt bad for everyone, from the drivers to the organizers to the people who gave up access to the park for this. But when the racing started happening, I noticed something. People came out. They emerged progressively as the laps ticked down. They cut holes in fences. They sat on the shoulders of fathers. They oohed and ahhed as the cars passed mere feet from where their asses were parked in lawn chairs.</p><section data-embed="pullquote" data-lazy-id="P0-15" data-node-id="26" class="embed"><blockquote class="css-18qhvnb e1pe3zr91"><span aria-hidden="true" class="css-0 eagam8p0"></span><blockquote class="css-gwp8ws e1pe3zr90">In a sport long-lampooned for “just going around in circles all day," it was phenomenal racing.</blockquote><span aria-hidden="true" class="css-0 eagam8p1"></span></blockquote></section><p data-journey-content="true" data-node-id="27" class="css-1nd4gv7 et3p2gv0">As for the course, it took a while for everyone to get used to it. Kyle Busch went deep into the tires, spilling collected water everywhere, and had to get pulled out. (He wouldn’t be the only one.) Several different drivers would take helm of the lead only to meet their demise on one tight 90-degree turn or another, the road slick with water: Christopher Bell, Tyler Reddick, Austin Dillon – each looked poised to take the prize at one point before the track said otherwise. Alex Bowman’s car caught on fire 20 feet from where I was standing.</p><section data-embed="x" data-lazy-id="P0-16" data-node-id="28" class="embed"><div data-embed="x"><section data-lazy-parent="P0-16" class="embed"><div data-embed="x" class="embed align-center css-10klw3m ez8lbhw1"><div class="css-63r9na ez8lbhw0"><img data-dynamic-svg="true" src="/web/20240301153637im_/https://www.roadandtrack.com/_assets/design-tokens/fre/static/icons/social/x.3361b6d.svg?primary=currentColor&amp;id=link-out-embed" loading="lazy" data-testid="dynamic-svg-base" height="auto" width="auto" alt="x" class="css-1msakm2 ez8lbhw2"/><a target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20240301153637/https://twitter.com/NASCARonNBC/status/1675662673613053956" aria-label="View full post on X" class="css-0 e1c1bym14">View full post on X</a></div></div></section></div></section><p data-journey-content="true" data-node-id="29" class="css-1nd4gv7 et3p2gv0">Not a single lap went by without something interesting happening – battles for position, huge gains made by those further back, pit row pileups, slideouts. It wasn’t just good racing in a sport long-lampooned for being “guys who just go around in circles all day” – it was phenomenal racing by any stretch of the imagination. </p><section data-embed="body-image" data-lazy-id="P0-17" data-node-id="30" class="embed"><div size="large" data-embed="body-image" class="align-center size-large embed css-d9wkvk e1xqj1sx4"><div class="css-uwraif e1xqj1sx3"><img alt="chicago, illinois july 02 the nascar safety crew assist kyle busch, driver of the 8 3chi chevrolet, after spinning into the safety tires during the nascar cup series grant park 220 at the chicago street course on july 02, 2023 in chicago, illinois photo by jared c tiltongetty images" title="NASCAR Cup Series Grant Park 220" loading="lazy" width="6000" height="4000" decoding="async" data-nimg="1" style="color:transparent;width:100%;height:auto;" sizes="100vw" srcset="https://web.archive.org/web/20240301153637im_/https://hips.hearstapps.com/hmg-prod/images/gettyimages-1509949634-64a43ac5d4f64.jpg?resize=640:* 640w, https://web.archive.org/web/20240301153637im_/https://hips.hearstapps.com/hmg-prod/images/gettyimages-1509949634-64a43ac5d4f64.jpg?resize=980:* 980w, https://web.archive.org/web/20240301153637im_/https://hips.hearstapps.com/hmg-prod/images/gettyimages-1509949634-64a43ac5d4f64.jpg?resize=1200:* 1120w, https://web.archive.org/web/20240301153637im_/https://hips.hearstapps.com/hmg-prod/images/gettyimages-1509949634-64a43ac5d4f64.jpg?resize=1200:* 1200w, https://web.archive.org/web/20240301153637im_/https://hips.hearstapps.com/hmg-prod/images/gettyimages-1509949634-64a43ac5d4f64.jpg?resize=2048:* 1920w" src="https://web.archive.org/web/20240301153637im_/https://hips.hearstapps.com/hmg-prod/images/gettyimages-1509949634-64a43ac5d4f64.jpg?resize=2048:*" class="css-0 evyp0mv0"/><div class="css-1gccgwy e1xqj1sx2"><figcaption class="css-1am3yn9 enfs9c50"><span class="css-cf5dap e6iqukd2">Jared C. Tilton</span></figcaption></div></div></div></section><p data-journey-content="true" data-node-id="31" class="css-1nd4gv7 et3p2gv0">The chaos produced huge upsets. Kyle Busch went from being in the tires to finishing 5th. Chase Elliot, who started 26th would, owing to a helluva lot of quick maneuvering, finish 3rd. Justin Haley, who struggled with the simulator, totaled his car in qualifying, and started the race dead last, finished in a jaw-dropping second place. But by far the biggest story was that of Kiwi Supercar driver Shane van Gisbergen, who pulled ahead of Haley in the twilight hours of the race and <a href="https://web.archive.org/web/20240301153637/https://www.roadandtrack.com/news/a44420000/shane-van-gisbergen-opened-the-floodgates/" target="_blank" data-vars-ga-outbound-link="https://www.roadandtrack.com/news/a44420000/shane-van-gisbergen-opened-the-floodgates/" data-vars-ga-ux-element="Hyperlink" data-vars-ga-call-to-action="won, astonishingly, in his Cup Series debut" class="body-link css-kji66a et3p2gv0">won, astonishingly, in his Cup Series debut</a>, something that hadn’t happened in NASCAR <em></em>since <em>1963</em>. There could not have been a better winner – the whole final lap had the aura of a fairytale. </p><section data-embed="body-image" data-lazy-id="P0-18" data-node-id="32" class="embed"><div size="large" data-embed="body-image" class="align-center size-large embed css-d9wkvk e1xqj1sx4"><div class="css-uwraif e1xqj1sx3"><img alt="chicago, illinois july 02 austin cindric, driver of the 2 discount tire ford, races during the nascar cup series grant park 220 at the chicago street course on july 02, 2023 in chicago, illinois photo by michael reavesgetty images" title="NASCAR Cup Series Grant Park 220" loading="lazy" width="4219" height="2812" decoding="async" data-nimg="1" style="color:transparent;width:100%;height:auto;" sizes="100vw" srcset="https://web.archive.org/web/20240301153637im_/https://hips.hearstapps.com/hmg-prod/images/gettyimages-1512837029-64a43df10e743.jpg?resize=640:* 640w, https://web.archive.org/web/20240301153637im_/https://hips.hearstapps.com/hmg-prod/images/gettyimages-1512837029-64a43df10e743.jpg?resize=980:* 980w, https://web.archive.org/web/20240301153637im_/https://hips.hearstapps.com/hmg-prod/images/gettyimages-1512837029-64a43df10e743.jpg?resize=1200:* 1120w, https://web.archive.org/web/20240301153637im_/https://hips.hearstapps.com/hmg-prod/images/gettyimages-1512837029-64a43df10e743.jpg?resize=1200:* 1200w, https://web.archive.org/web/20240301153637im_/https://hips.hearstapps.com/hmg-prod/images/gettyimages-1512837029-64a43df10e743.jpg?resize=2048:* 1920w" src="https://web.archive.org/web/20240301153637im_/https://hips.hearstapps.com/hmg-prod/images/gettyimages-1512837029-64a43df10e743.jpg?resize=2048:*" class="css-0 evyp0mv0"/><div class="css-1gccgwy e1xqj1sx2"><figcaption class="css-1am3yn9 enfs9c50"><span class="css-cf5dap e6iqukd2">Michael Reaves</span></figcaption></div></div></div></section><p data-journey-content="true" data-node-id="33" class="css-1nd4gv7 et3p2gv0">If you are NASCAR and you want to get new fans on board, this is the kind of racing that will do it. By the end of the evening, the energy was infectious. Everyone forgot about what a shitshow it was. This event is far from unsalvageable, despite the challenges. At the end of the day, if NASCAR has a pattern for success here – they should merely learn from what went right and what went wrong. In my opinion, all the Street Race needs to be a welcome and exciting perennial event is three things: better communication with the city and the transit agencies, more grandstands and other seating, and cheaper tickets. Open up Grant Park for $50 a pop and sell the seats for more. Forget the Chainsmokers. </p><section data-embed="body-image" data-lazy-id="P0-19" data-node-id="34" class="embed"><div size="large" data-embed="body-image" class="align-center size-large embed css-d9wkvk e1xqj1sx4"><div class="css-uwraif e1xqj1sx3"><img alt="chicago, illinois july 02 shane van gisbergen, driver of the 91 enhance health chevrolet, is congratulated by ross chastain, driver of the 1 adventhealth chevrolet, r victory lane after winning the nascar cup series grant park 220 at the chicago street course on july 02, 2023 in chicago, illinois photo by chris graythengetty images" https://web.archive.org/web/20240301153637im_/https://hips.hearstapps.com/hmg-prod/images/gettyimages-1510169931-64a43e196cd44.jpg?resize=980:* 980w, https://web.archive.org/web/20240301153637im_/https://hips.hearstapps.com/hmg-prod/images/gettyimages-1510169931-64a43e196cd44.jpg?resize=1200:* 1120w, e1xqj1sx2"><figcaption class="css-1am3yn9 enfs9c50"><span class="css-cf5dap e6iqukd2">Chris Graythen</span></figcaption><style data-emotion="css 48rem){.css-djjprz{line-height:1.3;}}@media(min-width: 40.625rem){.css-djjprz{line-height:1.3;}}@media(min-width: 64rem){.css-djjprz{line-height:1.3;}}.css-djjprz em,.css-djjprz metropolis.</div></div></div></div></section><p data-journey-content="true" data-node-id="35" class="css-1nd4gv7 et3p2gv0">As I left the track, I overheard dozens of spectators, most of whom were still buzzing from the night’s events. It’s true that many were from out of town – much was being said about catching a flight the next morning – but a lot of them were Chicagoans, discussing routes back home on the L. The one I remember most, though, was a five year old boy walking hand and hand with his mother. He asked her, “Mom, have you ever seen the Daytona 500 on TV?” His mother said she had. </p><p data-journey-content="true" data-node-id="36" class="css-1nd4gv7 et3p2gv0">“That’s so cool, mom,” the boy said. “That’s so cool.” </p><hr data-node-id="37" class="css-18pb4rg et3p2gv0"/><p data-journey-content="true" data-node-id="38" class="css-1nd4gv7 et3p2gv0"><em>Kate Wagner is a journalist and critic working in Chicago and Ljubljana, Slovenia. She covers topics ranging from architecture to culture to sports. As a sports journalist she has covered two Tours de France and numerous other races in professional cycling.</em></p><style data-emotion="css ciejky">.css-ciejky{clear:both;margin-top:1.25rem;}</style><div data-ad-exclude="true" id="journey-inline" class="css-ciejky e1cslvxz0"></div><style data-emotion="css The Street Race represents a bold new strategy, one that pulls from F1 courses like Monaco, capitalizing on a sport which is seeing a boom of popularity. It takes NASCAR, long considered a staple of the South (with all the cultural and political baggage wherein) and introduces it to a completely new, younger, and much more diverse audience. The diversity angle, namely the outreach toward Chicago’s Black community on the South Side was particularly emphasized by NASCAR’s community engagement events – for example, Bubba’s Block Party at the DuSable Museum of African American History. The message is clear: if the sport is to survive in the modern cultural consciousness, it needs to branch out, and fast. Many fans, including myself, assumed that a GA+ ticket included a seat in the grandstands. It did not. Those were reserved for ticket holders paying a frankly insane $465 and up, and there was nothing indicating that spectators should bring their own chairs. Things began to fill up when the Xfinity race started, only for it to be called off due to lightning strikes. The City of Chicago has a 90 minute waiting period for lightning compared to NASCAR’s 30. id="json-ld" type="application/ld+json">{"@type":"NewsArticle","thumbnailUrl":"https://web.archive.org/web/20240301153637/https://hips.hearstapps.com/hmg-prod/images/nascar-tire-flooding-64a455c1ba86f.jpg?crop=0.499xw:1.00xh;0.501xw,0&resize=100:*","datePublished":"2023-07-04T17:31:38.589139Z","headline":"NASCAR Needed Its Chicago Street Race to be a Success. Then Came the Flood.","articleBody":"Ross Chastain was awed by skyscrapers.Addressing the NASCAR press corps Friday at the Art Institute of Chicago, the Trackhouse Racing driver and recent winner of the Ally 400 said what we’d all been thinking: “It’s a little different than Nashville, that’s for sure…For me it's a bit different than Alva, Florida, too.”He looked out the window nervously.“You can't see the sky. It's only buildings. I see a couple trees and from my point of view right now. I'm not used to that. I'm used to wide open farm fields and two lane roads in South Florida. When I strap in, I'm probably not gonna see much of the sky. It's gonna be buildings and, and walls and fences and, and tight confines.”Chastain, a spicy, dynamic driver and the heir to a watermelon-farming family off Florida’s Gulf Coast, was right to be anxious. His anxiety was reflected everywhere the race touched, from the drivers, to the city government, to NASCAR itself, to fans, to the people who live in Chicago and commute downtown, their day woefully disrupted. I think it’s fair to call the Chicago Street Race, which took place Saturday July 1st through Sunday July 3rd, an experiment. A big, risky experiment. For NASCAR, a lot was riding on this event going smoothly. The Street Race represents a bold new strategy, one that pulls from F1 courses like Monaco, capitalizing on a sport which is seeing a boom of popularity. It takes NASCAR, long considered a staple of the South (with all the cultural and political baggage wherein) and introduces it to a completely new, younger, and much more diverse audience. The diversity angle, namely the outreach toward Chicago’s Black community on the South Side was particularly emphasized by NASCAR’s community engagement events – for example, Bubba’s Block Party at the DuSable Museum of African American History. The message is clear: if the sport is to survive in the modern cultural consciousness, it needs to branch out, and fast. Pulling from F1 is probably a good place to start. Jenson Button, 2009 F1 champion-cum-NASCAR driver, would know better than most. “I can only think of positives,” he said in the press conference. “We're trying something new…I know from previous experiences, street races for the teams, for the drivers, it's all a big learning curve.” For Button, Chicago is just the beginning. “I want to see racing in Europe. I think the European fans are very on board with NASCAR at the moment, especially after the performance that we had at Le Mans. They're new fans and I think that's one thing about racing in the streets here.”That’s the drivers’ side of the story. For Chicago, the situation is more complicated. The NASCAR Street Race was a project of the outgoing mayor, Lori Lightfoot, and since its inception has been criticized by community activists and transportation advocates around the city.“We were deeply concerned about the lack of transparency here. And transit seemed like an afterthought. Safety seemed like an afterthought,” said David Powe, who works at the Active Transportation Alliance, a transit nonprofit. “The economy and tourism should never come before human safety, air quality and the equity concerns of making sure that people using the bus can get to where they're trying to get to healthcare, get to school, get to their medical appointments, get to a grocery store. We're just deeply concerned about the previous administration's push to get this approved and scheduled.”“Chicagoans have been calling for better access to our public parks, whether that's Riis Park or Grant Park, Millennium Park or the Lakefront Trail. And [instead] we've just been giving more and more of our public space away to corporations. This is just another one of those examples,” said Rony Islam, an organizer with Chicago Bike Grid Now! “NASCAR talks a lot about like, oh, I'm doing community outreach, and they've got like a section of their setup that's open to the public or whatever. But it's not really open to the public and it's not open to all Chicagoans. And when you look at their ticket prices, for example, oh yeah. It's very clear that it's not open to all Chicagoans.”Islam has a point. At $269 and up, the tickets, in fact, do not come cheap. Even for NASCAR, they’re deeply expensive, and the organization hoped that by combining the race with a kind of half music festival – acts like The Black Crows and the Chainsmokers were to perform – would justify the cost of entry. If NASCAR wants to reach out to a more diverse fanbase, $269 is a little high if you’re a college student or working a 9-to-5. Regardless of the lack of transparency, the turning of Grant Park into a fortress, and the high costs, the event would go on regardless. The big experiment was on. Then the flood came.Things weren’t ideal before it started raining on Saturday. “It’s giving Fyre Festival,” I overheard a fan say waiting in line for a $10 Busch Light in the General Admission Plus zone, which gave one access to a bunch of strewn about picnic tables and bathrooms that weren’t porta potties. Lots of things were already coming apart by the time I got there during the Xfinity Cup practice round on Saturday. Many fans, including myself, assumed that a GA+ ticket included a seat in the grandstands. It did not. Those were reserved for ticket holders paying a frankly insane $465 and up, and there was nothing indicating that spectators should bring their own chairs. The sophisticated Tap to Pay bracelet system didn’t work. By 2 p.m., when the first show started, Grant Park was virtually empty. I’ve been to house shows with more people. Things began to fill up when the Xfinity race started, only for it to be called off due to lightning strikes. The City of Chicago has a 90 minute waiting period for lightning compared to NASCAR’s 30. Eventually, everyone was sent home and the Chainsmokers concert was canceled.It got worse. Chicago has been suffering from a severe drought for months, only for the heavens to open beginning Sunday morning. Flash Flood warnings swept in around the city with explicit instructions: DO NOT LEAVE YOUR POSITION UNLESS YOU ARE SEEKING SAFER GROUND. Images from the racetrack started to pour (pun intended) in from Twitter. Tires floating in puddles. Inches of water standing on the asphalt. First the hammer came for the musical acts. Then the resumption of the Xfinity Race, leaving Cole Custer declared the winner in a rare race called before the end of \"stage 2.\" All eyes were on the Cup Series, which entered a holding pattern at least until the rain stopped and the track could be squeegeed. In the replies to each news update were fans demanding a refund, as the musical acts and other perks were the only advantage they had over those folks crowding around balconies and peeking through the holes in fences. Cameras panned towards empty grandstands and drivers standing around in ankle-high water. It was, to put it bluntly, a disaster for NASCAR. When the news came that they’d try to race – doing a few single-file laps under caution to give the drivers the final say – the sun emerged from the clouds. By the time I got down to the track, people had gathered in ponchos, skeptical and burned out. The grounds were one giant puddle, the sidewalks caked with mud. Honestly, I felt bad for everyone, from the drivers to the organizers to the people who gave up access to the park for this. But when the racing started happening, I noticed something. People came out. They emerged progressively as the laps ticked down. They cut holes in fences. They sat on the shoulders of fathers. They oohed and ahhed as the cars passed mere feet from where their asses were parked in lawn chairs.As for the course, it took a while for everyone to get used to it. Kyle Busch went deep into the tires, spilling collected water everywhere, and had to get pulled out. (He wouldn’t be the only one.) Several different drivers would take helm of the lead only to meet their demise on one tight 90-degree turn or another, the road slick with water: Christopher Bell, Tyler Reddick, Austin Dillon – each looked poised to take the prize at one point before the track said otherwise. Alex Bowman’s car caught on fire 20 feet from where I was standing.Not a single lap went by without something interesting happening – battles for position, huge gains made by those further back, pit row pileups, slideouts. It wasn’t just good racing in a sport long-lampooned for being “guys who just go around in circles all day” – it was phenomenal racing by any stretch of the imagination. The chaos produced huge upsets. Kyle Busch went from being in the tires to finishing 5th. Chase Elliot, who started 26th would, owing to a helluva lot of quick maneuvering, finish 3rd. Justin Haley, who struggled with the simulator, totaled his car in qualifying, and started the race dead last, finished in a jaw-dropping second place. But by far the biggest story was that of Kiwi Supercar driver Shane van Gisbergen, who pulled ahead of Haley in the twilight hours of the race and won, astonishingly, in his Cup Series debut, something that hadn’t happened in NASCAR since 1963. There could not have been a better winner – the whole final lap had the aura of a fairytale. If you are NASCAR and you want to get new fans on board, this is the kind of racing that will do it. By the end of the evening, the energy was infectious. Everyone forgot about what a shitshow it was. This event is far from unsalvageable, despite the challenges. At the end of the day, if NASCAR has a pattern for success here – they should merely learn from what went right and what went wrong. In my opinion, all the Street Race needs to be a welcome and exciting perennial event is three things: better communication with the city and the transit agencies, more grandstands and other seating, and cheaper tickets. Open up Grant Park for $50 a pop and sell the seats for more. Forget the Chainsmokers. As I left the track, I overheard dozens of spectators, most of whom were still buzzing from the night’s events. It’s true that many were from out of town – much was being said about catching a flight the next morning – but a lot of them were Chicagoans, discussing routes back home on the L. The one I remember most, though, was a five year old boy walking hand and hand with his mother. He asked her, “Mom, have you ever seen the Daytona 500 on TV?” His mother said she had. “That’s so cool, mom,” the boy said. “That’s so cool.” Kate Wagner is a journalist and critic working in Chicago and Ljubljana, Slovenia. She covers topics ranging from architecture to culture to sports.
